<Author>meblake
<Content>Boutique hotel with a great location My partner and I stayed there for 3 days over the New Years holiday. The hotel is in a fantastic location, right off Market Street and close to Union Square. We booked a great rate through Orbitz and paid $160 per night. Check-in was fast. The room was fairly basic but clean. It's very similar in style to the W Hotel brand. The bathrooms are a bit dated and could stand to be renovated. Our room was on a lower floor, near the elevators, and did not have much of a view. We would've preferred a better room but I'm sure the low rate we paid had an impact on our placement. The complimentary wi-fi in the rooms is a nice touch. There's no real lobby bar (or even much of a lobby) due to its layout. We usally like to have a couple drinks at the hotel we're staying out before we go out to dinner or after a long day of sightseeing.Service at the hotel was great. The staff is younger and very friendly. We checked in on New Year's Eve and the staff suggested walking down to the Embaradero to watch fireworks which was a great idea.We had lunch at the Slanted Door in the Ferry Building and would definitely recommend it. It always has great food and nice atmosphere. There's always a wait there so make reservations if you know you want to eat there.On our last night, the concierge made a reservation for us at North Beach Restaurant and got us a town car service for transportation. Great food and speedy service (maybe even a little too quick if you're looking for a leisurely meal). During the meal, my partner noticed he had misplaced his cell phone, possibly in the car. When we arrived back at the hotel, the doorman asked if we had lost a phone and produced it immediately. Very nice touch!I'd recommend the hotel if you're looking for something that's reasonably priced, in a great location, and has a little bit of style. If I stayed there again, I'd suggest trying to book a better category room, on a higher floor, and with a view of Market Street.

<Author>cmgparsons
<Content>Super hotel, super location After spending endless hours searching online for a *good* price for a long weekend in San Francisco, I came across a short mention of the Hotel Palomar in Travel  Leisure magazine. This is a wonderful hotel in a great location. We had a lovely room, a bit small, but extremely comfortable with all of the amenities....even l'Occitane products in the bathroom. Nice comfy bed with crisp white down duvet.....very much appreciated after cross-country flight, then lots of walking in fun San Francisco. We faced the courtyard so the room was very quiet. Even the hallways, elevators,  public spaces were spotlessly clean  everything smelled so fresh. (After all, it is in a city!) Only negative was the snooty restaurant, but there are lots of dining options nearby....Mel's Diner for breakfast and Annabelle's for late nite dinner. And if you can't find something to eat in foodie heaven (aka San Francisco) there's something wrong with you! The parking was expensive  we agreed that you really don't need a car there. Definitely would return. And the price was the best part......$195 a night. Most city hotels there are double that!

<Author>RockyMountain2
<Content>Nice Hotel, Good Location My partner and I stayed at the Palomar over a long weekend while visiting friends in SF. I had never stayed there before, but knew of the hotel from previously living in SF. I received a great package deal price that included parking. (Booked through Kimpton's website directly.) For the level of hotel, it was the least expensive parking package I could find at comparable hotels in the city. It was a good deal.The staff was very friendly, helpful, and the accommodations very nice. I would recommend this hotel. Be sure to request a high floor, because of street noise. We were on the 8th floor and this was not an issue. The staff at checkout had some issues with our bill and charged an incorrect amount. Be sure to check your bill. However, this was just a mistake by a new staff person. It happens. Given the price and location, I would stay here again and recommend the Palomar. You have easy access to MUNI, BART, and Union Square.

<Content>Hotel Palomar - Absolutely Awesome! We stayed here for a short weekend trip, and would definately stay here again for a longer trip next time. It was our first time staying at the Hotel Palomar or at any Kimpton Hotel. We decided on this hotel because it was pet friendly and we had our two dogs with us for the weekend. We booked our room through the hotel's reservations directly because they were able to give us a better deal than all the other travel websites. Would highly recommend that you contact the hotel and see what their best available prices are before you book your rooms via Expedia or Orbitz, etc. The minute we pulled up to the front, we were instantly greeted and helped out. They also greeted our puppies which made us felt very welcomed. When we were checking in, the people at the front desk even gave our pups doggie treats. We had heard great things of a Thai restaurant but we couldn't remember the name exactly so we asked the gentlemen that was helping us with the check-in. He instantly looked up the name of the restaurant for us, and even helped us make reservations for the night! The location of the hotel makes going everywhere super convenient too....it's right in the heart of downtown, Union Square. We had a car with us so we had it valeted for the weekend. The hotel parks the car in their indoor parking lot located downstairs of the hotel, which is great because we didn't have to worry about the car being in an outdoor lot. Oh, and did I mention the complimentary wine hour!?!! The hotel hosts a complimentary wine hour where they introduce a red wine and white wine for their guests to try! Our overall experience was just absolutely awesome. The hotel is super accommodating, the staff were all very professional, and friendly. LOVED IT! Highly recommend it, hands down.

<Author>QQ2008
<Content>Lovely - Great value - Some communication issues Great rate on Travelzoo.com - $139.00 for two doubles. Nick-Dal thought room was small, but perhaps has never stayed in a NYC 85 sf shoebox boutique hotel for $350 ... our Palomar room was HUGE! Well appointed, comfortable (except for the pillows; I dislike down, and the foam pillows that were brought up were hard as rocks). Staff was very friendly, but it took forever for them to bring our bags to the room. (Three calls to the desk and one personal trip to look for them; apparently there was one bellman on duty and couldn't deal with several people checking in at once ... we were late for an appointment because of that. When he finally did deliver the bags he said there would be a bottle of wine delivered to our room for our trouble, but the wine never materialized.) Towels were not changed daily, which didn't bother me, but it did bother my travel companion (there was no note in the bathroom indicating that towels would not be changed, as I've seen in other hotels). Didn't eat in the hotel restaurant, so can't comment on that. Annabelle's Bistro just down the block had one of the best Ceasar Salads that I've ever tasted. Hotel offers a free wine tasting daily from 5-6, which is a lovely idea, but we were out sightseeing all day, and never in our hotel at that hour. Would have been a nice end to the day at 9 pm or so. Overall, good experience at the Palomar. Very clean, comfortable, friendly and quiet.

<Author>amarion
<Content>Excellent Hotel and Location This Hotel is situated at the perfect location right in the heart of downtown San Francisco. You are 2 blocks to Union Square, 1/2 a block to BART, 6 blocks to China Town, 2 blocks to the famous Cable Cars.The hotel is decorated nicely, very clean and the service is quick and efficient. Our check in took about 2 minutes and we were upgraded to a huge room overlooking market street. We were concerned about the street noise, but it was very quiet and a great place to people watch out the windows.The room had a large, King bed with bench in front, a seating area with table to the side and another seating area by the bedside. It had a huge flatscreen tv on the wall with DVD player and pay movies. It also had HBO.The bathroom was very spacious with lots of granite counter space and was very clean. There was a large closet in the room with ironing board and plenty of storage.We used the fitness room in the hotel, which was very small and a bit crowded when 2 other people came into it. It was convenient though, because most hotels in the area make you go to outside locations to excercise, which is really a hassle.My only small complaint was the lack of comfort from the pillows. They were very soft and mushy and made sleeping a bit difficult. After mentioning this in an online survey from Kimpton Hotels, the manager replied right away and apologized for the pillows and said to contact him next time I was coming to town and he'd upgrade my room. I thought that was excellent service.

<Author>WebBrown

The hotel rooms are small but nice. So if you are looking for lots of space, look else where. The room has a desk, bed, flat screen t.v. and an updated bathroom. I would stay here again if I was in the area. Of of course I was here for business and received a rate of $199/night, which was less than half of what they normally charge. <Author>Raf1966
<Content>Super Spot I stayed here for 5 nights on business. The location was absolutely superb. I took the BART in from the airport and it was barely 5 mins walk which is easy these days with with suitcase you can pull behind you. I also took the BART back when i left. Its so easy and just $5. The room was furnished in traditional old style but was warm and welcoming. There was plenty of space and a good desk which was important for me. The internet access was excellent and free. The bathroom was a little dated but it worked fine and the L'occitane products never fail to help.They didn't have tea making facilities and it took 3 goes to get a kettle up to the room. I guess my Spanish is useless. Other than that the room was great. No noise to speak of even though its in a busy location. The breakfast was in a meeting room as they were refurbishing the main hotel restaurant and bar which was a shame. it was average but they had fresh fruit which is always great. The staff were friendly and helpful and the hotel had a general impression of being tailored for business/tourists. The location was great for getting around. The Apple store was just across the road and Union Square a stones throw. I didn't have any room service but there is a great little french bistro 5 doors down on the right which i recommend highly. i ate there twice on my own and really enjoyed the food. also another block down on the right is a good cafe serving breakfast and nice juices for a quick start.I'd stay there again as was good value, good location and overall a tidy place.

<Author>tkelly7
<Content>Excellent choice I had to come to San Francisco for a conference at the Marriott downtown. Because I prefer to stay in smaller hotels, I booked the Palomar which is right across the street from the Marriott. I couldn't have been happier with the experience. The staff was welcoming and very helpful, the room was spacious and comfortable. My first night they sent a plate of fresh fruit to my room. And the price was only $10 more than what I would have paid at the Marriott. The hotel is just two blocks from the SF MOMA and at a public transportation nexus (BART, tram, cable cars).My only complaint is that eating in the hotel is quite expensive ($6 Rice Crispies). So I ate out the entire time. For cheap eats to go, I recommend the Alexandria Cafe or the Coffee Bean around the corner one way on Market. Or the Westfield Mall food court around the corner on Market the other way. It sounds cheesy to eat in a mall food court, but this is a very upscale mall and the food was excellent and a full meal could be had for around $10. The King of Thai Noodles on the opposite side of the block from the hotel is also excellent and reasonably priced.I will stay here every time I come to San Francisco from now on.

<Content>pleasant stay! unfortunately chosen a wrong rainy season to visit, the the hotel staff and the location are some of the things to make my trip wonderful.having said that, on the other side is that we have enjoyed sf with less tourist, it's like the whole city is yours.me and my partner absolutely loved the decor of the hotel, it's simple, modern, and mostly, very clean; we were upgraded right away to the exec. floor; that is true, sf is such a small city, and it does not matter where you stay; the hotel is in the heart of downtown, union sq. is also all surrounded by christmas display, the hotel is actually facing a quieter street, so it is in the center of the city, yet it is actually very quiet.do not hesitate to ask the wonderful hotel staff regarding any questions, and luckily they are all also with great taste to tell you where is the hottest spot in town.few suggestions: def do the alcatraz night tour, we were all surprised with the spooky atmosphere at night, they also provide partially free guided tour; strongly recommended reservation for all the great restaurant, i mean book them before the trip; the hayes street, the best place to eat, shop, and ppl watching, ignore union street, dated shops but great place to find food; the wonderful food court in westfield mall, yes, a food court, and it is a 5 star hotel like food court where you can find all types of food. again, sf is a small city, do not plan to do one section (i.e. ashbury, soma) in one day, you can easily finish few of them all together, so def plan an escape or two during the trip, either wine tasting or muir woods, they are actually fun!

<Author>imperator12
<Content>Needs an overhaul, but still a pleasant place to stay The Palomar brand is now popping up all across the country; my first experience was with the exceedingly glamorous Palomar in Washington, DC. Last year I booked a room at the Palomar in San Francisco and have since made it my preferred hotel in that city.The SF Palomar is NOT glamorous. It may have been when it first opened but it is now definitely showing its age. The decor is firmly rooted in a mid-1990's aesthetic. Nonetheless, it is well maintained and I still find the lobby (except for the battered sofa) and elevator vestibules to be quite attractive. The rooms could use an update. They are very comfortable but definitely bland. The cream-colored walls really wash-out the rooms and no amount of brightly colored accessories can alleviate the drabness.And that's pretty much the only negative I have for the place. The rooms may be dull in decor--and a bit too snug at times--but the comfort factor is high. The beds and linen encourages one to sleep-in on rainy San Francisco mornings. The bathrooms are non-descript, but they work and I've always had plenty of hot water when I needed it. Housekeeping is gracious (Marina leaves me cute notes) and very efficient. The picture windows in the rooms facing Market Street are well insulated against the noise generated by the pandemonium below. However, those who are particularly sensitive to outside noise may prefer one of the inside rooms; they have an almost tomb-like quality.The location is great. The Pal is right on the corner of Market and 4th, just a very short walk away from the epicenter of the best shopping on the west coast. If you're lucky, you'll get one of the precious few outside rooms. The windows are huge and it's fun watching all the scurrying below; society ladies with Armani bags, protesters, backpackers, Buddhist monks, guys in drag, street performers, investment bankers, and seemingly every other example of humanity all collide together right outside the hotel. Another big plus is that the Powell Street MUNI/BART station is right around the corner from the Palomar's entrance. The Pal is great for museum junkies (like me); the spectacular DeYoung is a MUNI ride away and the Museum of Modern Art is just a ten minute walk from the Pal's doors. The Palomar has an interesting advantage in that it's located next door to the Westfield Mall. During my first few visits to the hotel, the staff would direct me to the Westfield's food court when I asked where I could get a quick bite to eat. I initially scoffed at the idea of getting a meal at a food court but this is no ordinary food court. The Korean BBQ joint is quick, cheap, and so very delicious. Corriander, right next to it, has wonderful Thai food at bargain prices. I truly enjoy grabbing a meal at the Westfield food court and bringing it back to my room to watch a movie (the rooms at the Palomar are equipped with DVD players.) One time I asked one of the front desk people (I shall not name the person) about room service; the person just shook his head and mouthed the words You don't want to do that. That pretty well sums up the quality of the Palomar's room service. The Pal has a very formal restaurant called the Fifth Floor. It's very good but for a truly awesome meal in an achingly romantic setting ask Stephen, the concierge, to get you reservations at Chez Spencer.Which brings me to the Palomar's most shining asset: the staff. These people are no corporate drones; they are charming, wacky, funny, and vibrant. They are also very competant at what they do. I'm away from home quite a bit and almost always travel by myself; it is such a luxury to walk into a hotel and be welcomed back as an old friend. Overall, if you want up-to-date style go to the W. If you need pampered luxury--and are willing to pay dearly for it--go to the Mandarin Oriental. The Palomar is for those who place comfort above trendy luxury and who appreciate a warm, welcoming staff. And the Pal's location just cannot be beat if you're in SF for shopping, clubbing and/or museum hopping.  
<Date>Dec 20, 2007

<Author>georgiabd
<Content>Nice boutique hotel My husband and I recently visited San Fran for the first time. We spent two nights at the Palomar. It's a nice, small boutique hotel. The staff was very welcoming upon check-in. Our room was modern and clean. It had a very small shower and a large soaking tub. Nice honor bar and bath products. For us, the location was just so-so. It's VERY near shopping but we would probably stay in Nob Hill next time. The restaurant, Fifth Floor, is very nice and chic. We had breakfast there both days. Great lox and bagels. It's supposed to be great for dinner. My one major complaint about the Palomar is that there wasn't a dedicated concierge on duty. The front desk staff were friendly but weren't able to recommend good restaurants and make compairsons among them for us. Also, there seems to be a taxi shortage in the area so we had problems getting one for dinner. The Palomar lacks the large hotel atmosphere of a lobby bar, music, etc. but we had a very nice stay.

<Author>PlanesTrainsAutos4
<Content>Nice Place, Great Location I wouldn't classify this hotel as luxury but it's definitely an excellent choice. The location is fantastic, right near the corner of Fourth and Market so if shopping is your main reason for going to SF, you are going to be right in the thick of it. As a boutique hotel, the lobby is small which is fine with me... if you want to drop of f packages or make a stop up to your room you don't have to meander through a huge lobby, wait for an elevator, etc. The room was small with an interior view (overlooked the escalators in the Old Navy store below) but comfy and the space in the room was utilized very well, loved the bedding and the L'Occitane toiletries. No problems with the shower either... this is a big deal for me... enough hot water and good water pressure. The staff is friendly and professional. There were cold drinks in the lobby throughout the day and they serve coffee there in the a.m. - no coffee maker in the room unless you request one. If you have a car, there is parking under the hotel (really expensive) or you can park around the corner in the Fifth  Mission garage for a bit less (I think it was about $28 a day?). There is a movie theater right across the street (The Metreon) and a Marriott is also across the street. We went up to the 39th floor there at night for a drink and a fabulous view. Great breakfast at Mel's Diner (yes, the one from American Graffiti) around the corner on Mission St. The Palomar has a lounge as well and a restaurant, but unfortunately we didn't get a chance to check either one out. The restaurant had excellent reviews. Our rate at this hotel was about $180 a night which I thought was reasonable. I would stay here again for sure.

<Author>frequenttraveller100
<Content>Surperb for business travelers Just returned from a five day business trip to SF. We needed to be close to downtown businesses off Market Street with Govt Rates. Few hotels had availability even several months ago when we booked. It is the height of the tourist season afterall.We chose the Hotel Palomar based on other TripAdvisor reviews. Good choice. We had two rooms--atrium room was very light and quiet. Street rooms are noisy on lower floors; fine above five or six. Atrium room and bath was exceptionally large; other was small and tight with two beds. Handicapped bathroom was without a walk or roll in shower. However, the excess of grab bars made it useable. The staff ARE very attentive. We especially enjoyed and visited with the Head Bell Man, the doormen and the security men on in the evenings. Because we were there a full week they got to know us, and our comings and goings. They made the best suggestions. Concierge service was adequate, but not very experienced or with first hand knowledge. Often they relied on reports or questions from prior guests all stored in the hotel computer. They did suggest a 12 person van tour of the wine country for us that I also recommend--Pacific Tours. Although the hotel was short-staffed in housekeeping, what ever we asked for at the front desk was promptly received or corrected--too few bath towels for two, more soap, change the hypoallergic pillows, etc. Yes the low flush toilets are noisy...they all are. Yes the lobby is minimal--but there is a lovely quiet sitting area on the fifth floor which we used nightly for business meetings. We could even have a drink or order soup or lite fare during our meetings. My mom sat out there with a friend one day while the room was being made up. Yes, the restaurant is pricey. But it is totally in line with any other top flight restaurant in SF. It is rated THE BEST French restaurant in the city. Nearby is Annabelle's which is reasonable and the food is very good. Note Annabelle's has a restaurant and a bar menu that are totally different. Also nearby in the Westfield Mall is a food court with all types of ethnic and uncommon fare at low or more typical SF prices. In the mornings we used the hotel car service to go to our work location. Ideal with our brief cases and computers, we went door to door at low cost and maximum convenience. That should be arranged with the door man in advance. The service is first come first serve on weekdays. Our rooms were exceptionally clean, comfortable, and the location cannot be beat. It is about two blocks from Moscone Center too. I recommend the Palomar to every moderate priced business traveller. They had free wi-fi too.

<Author>ewe35
<Content>Good Hotel near the Moscone Center We recently stayed at the Palomar when I went to the SF Gift Show at the Moscone Center. The location is great! The hotel itself was quite good. The rate was a special show rate of $185 per night and it was worth it. There was a problem worth noting, however.  We checked in late and the desk staff is very casual, a tad unprofessional, I would say. We had a requested a king bed and that was not available , So they said, we can give you a king bed in a suite but it will cost $150 more per night. I was pretty tired so I said okay for tonight. The suite was a real suite, but really nothing special, certainly not worth $150 more. Anyway, the next day we switched to a standard room with a king bed, which was then avaialble. The whole thing was annoying. We had requested the king bed and even confirmed it a few days before.  I am happy to report that when I checked out, the woman at the front desk, immediately deleted the $150 charge as soon as I explained the story. She was a pleasure to deal with and it left me with a really good feeling about the Palomar. Other than that, the room was very nice. The hotel is very clean and the lobby restaurant breakfast is quite good-not cheap, but these sort of places rarely are. But the restaurant is very comfortable and the service is good.The fitness center is merely a treadmill and a stepper or two, so don't expect much. All in all, a good hotel.

<Author>enofile1
<Content>Great-If At the Right Price The Hotel Palomar, a member of the Klimpton Hotel Group, was reputed to be a luxurious representative of this prolific chain. Although the Palomar was very pleasant, I would not call it a luxury hotel.The lobby is quite tiny and guests take one of two small elevators up to their rooms. There are a few chairs in the lobby, and a coffee urn is left out all day for guests use.The rooms were a nice size with pleasant furnishings that were quite understated and calm for a Klimpton hotel. The bathroom was comfortable, but just like the room, nothing I would call luxurious.The staff were quite nice and tried to be helpful, but the Concierge did cop a bit of an attitude when asked about restaurants and bars even though I gave him a twenty dollar tip. I never did ask him to make a reservation for me.The restaurant is one of the most expensive in San Francisco and was rather stiff for this progressive city. The lofty ambiance of the restaurant did not match the pedestrian design of the hotel rooms.The location is excellent if you want to be near SOMA and Union Square. However, if you know San Francisco, the hotel's location on Market Street means that you will encounter the street people that are an integral part of the fabric of this city. (The entrance of the hotel is on Fourth Street)The health club can hardly be called that since it consists of a few pieces of equipment that are right on top of each other. I think my perspiration was spraying everyone in the room!The Hotel Palomar is a very nice hotel, but it is lacking certain elements that would bring it into the luxury reign of hotels.

<Author>michbren
<Content>WONDERFUL HOTEL!! My husband and I recently spent six nights at the Hotel Palomar. There was an initial problem with the reservation but it was handled promptly, professionally and much to our satisfaction. As with most Kimpton hotels the room was impeccibly clean and nicely appointed. Daily the room was cleaned perfectly, was done very promptly and caused no inconvenience to us. The nightly turn down service is nice. Although our room looked out over Market Street, we heard no noise, nor did we hear other guests inside. The beds were great and the linens are fantastic. Newspapers that were requested were delivered early each morning. As pointed out in previous reviews the lobby is very, very small (about three adults can sit in it). The staff at the desk was very professional, but we did not have any dealings with them except for check-in and check-out. This hotel is a great peaceful escape after running around San Francisco all day. The location is great and the lobby exits on Fourth Street right at a very busy bus stop. We were able to walk to Union Square several times, the Curran Theatre and Yerba Buena Gardens. The BART Powell St station is less than a half a block away. The Westfield Shopping Center is right next door. I am not a shopping-type person but that is a must-see. What a gorgeous mall!!The only negatives we felt were the size of the fitness room (very small with one treadmill and limited weights). I know you can go to another fitness facilty down the street but it is much more convenient when you can use the hotel's fitness center. We missed the nightly wine gatherings that we have enjoyed at other Kimpton hotels. It is so nice to relax with other guests, but the Hotel Palomar does not offer that amenity. The restaurant dinner menu was very different -- not what most people would eat. It is obvious they know this since the dining room is very small and never crowded. We had breakfast there a couple of times and it was very good. We would definitely recommend this hotel for the high quality and great location that it has. Kimpton does a very nice job taking care of their guests in a subtle way.  
<Date>Jul 26, 2007

<Author>CanadianBoys
<Content>Great Location - Average Place We just got back from SF and stayed at the Hotel Palomar for 3 nights (F/S/S). The location of the hotel is very good, near Union Stn and adjacent to Moscone Centre. We checked in late (around midnight) and found the front desk staff to be rather informal and questioned our reservation requirements. Although I had requested an Exec Room we were not provided one, and were given a standard room with feather pillows when my profile says synthetic due to allergies. In the morning asked for a different room. We were provided an Exec Room and the pillows were replaced to meet our request. At 315 sq ft, the Exec Room is small for 2 people, and pretty basis. Dcor is straight out of Ikea. The hotel itself has no real amenities and the lobby is very small - so small that when we checked out, people crowded into the street out front ?which by the way has street people and a bus stop. There is no bar, coffee area etc. on the main floor lobby level. We would stay again here, but only if the rate was very good as it does not warrant 4 star pricing. We rate this place as 3.5 stars - due to lack of amenities in the hotel itself, inadequate lobby, and lack of attention to details of reservation made. One final note: we stored out luggage for a while on checkout and it took 30 minutes to have it retrieved ?so watch your time.

<Author>karenandjeff
<Content>Not good for families We were very excited to enter the Hotel Palomar. It's very sleek and in the middle of everything. Upon arrival, they gave us a room across from the Restaurant. They told us it wouldn't be a problem, we wouldn't hear a thing. Tell that to our children who heard the reception going on in the lounge. The other problem is the way the rooms are set up. They're very sleek with great design -- unless you want a dresser, and extra nightstand or a closet large enough to put your clothes. When we asked for a dresser, we were told we'd have to upgrade to a suite for an additional $200+ a night. After a bit, they did offer to put a dresser from storage in our room, but weren't sure it would really fit. In addition, the bathroom didn't have a lock -- which is fine for a couple, but a family of 4, 2 of them being curious boys, that doesn't work. Lastly, the towels. The first night we asked for 2 more sets since we were a family of four. We kept on having to ask for more towels. The request wan't automatically made for us. There is coffee service in the morning -- but no food, unless you want to eat at the VERY formal restaurant. On the up side, the staff was VERY nice and helpful.

<Author>WorldtravelerMPLS
<Content>A terrific, stylish shopper's hotel A few years ago I visited San Francisco and I walked by an extra nice hotel and noted the Palomar name. Last month I finally got around to staying there.From SF International Airport to the center of town you can take a cab, a shuttle, a bus or BART. I chose the Bay Area Rapid Transit System (BART) as my method of reaching central San Franciso because all I had to drag on wheels was my carry-on bag. The fare was $5.10 or $5.20. It takes half an hour. As you go up the esculator from the Powell Street station you can see the sign for the Palomar. Can't beat that. Half a block walk and you are there. Map it online ahead of time. I was early for my reservation but the staff got me directed to my room. It faced away from the street and over a glass atrium. It was also a bit cramped. I could be in any hotel in the country with this view. I went back to the lobby and asked for a better room. For $20.00 a night more I got a slightly larger room that overlooked Market Street, a main San Franciso street. Granted I did hear some street musicians through the window in the evening but stuff like this stops at around 10 PM. I had three quiet nights of sleep.I can't say enough nice things about the staff. Want an opinion about a restaurant? You can get several. It happens that the historic, reasonably priced John's Grill is only a couple of blocks away. As for the room again. It was clean.No walk-in shower but a nice bath. Nice, light cover for the bed so you can see how clean it is.Kind of weird to have two desk chairs. Great if you are going to have a couple of visitors to your room.Reading lights for bed reading could be better (as with most hotels).Mattress was comfortable as were the pillows.NY Times delivered to the door. At check out I was told I could have gotten a SF paper if I had told them.I have to admit that the room didn't have any cutting edge design features like I have seen in Park Hyatts or Westins but it had a nice contemporay look and I felt it was a notch higher than the standard HIlton, domestic Radisson or Sheraton.

<Author>dephal
<Content>Positive experience at the Palomar My daughter and I just returned from a 1 night stay at the Palomar, and we really enjoyed it.We got a great rate from the hotel's website--$140 for a Saturday night (plus parking, which is expensive). The staff was really nice. When we first arrived, a bevy of 3 or 4 people ran up to help us. The staff paid special attention to my daughter, who's 7. The desk clerk actually encouraged her to jump on the bed, and the doorman jokingly chided her for not wearing a jacket. Despite the good service, none of the staff seems to particularly expect tips, and they seem genuinely thankful when they do receive them.The room was quite large and attractive, and the beds very comfortable. We were on the 8th floor and had a very nice view across Market Street and up toward Union Square. The L'Occitane amenities are nice, too.The location is really fantastic--BART and MUNI stop downstairs, great shopping is steps away, and SFMOMA and other museums are just a short walk away. I don't like this hotel quite as much as another Kimpton Hotel in SF, the Argonaut, but the Palomar's location is superior (unless you want to be at Fisherman's Wharf).The room was quiet in that we didn't hear a peep from neighboring rooms or the hallway. However, at 8pm a band set up across the street, and it was quite audible, even through the double-paned windows. We didn't mind, but if you don't want to hear Jimi Hendrix tunes until 11 pm (plus the occasional siren and other street noise) ask for an interior room.I only have a couple small complaints. 1. The bathroom has a pocket door. These seem to be popular in SF hotels, but I don't like them. 2. The lobby, although attractive, is small. Unlike other Kimpton properties, I don't think this one has a free wine hour in the evening. 3. I'm a Kimpton In-Touch member, but didn't get the usual welcome amenity.

<Author>Bobert1
<Content>my home in SF My favorite in SF. I've enjoyed at least 10 stays at the Palomar over 8 years. The only reason I ever stay elsewhere is if I can't get a good rate there. It's often not cheap, but it's worth it to keep checking for a low rate. To be fair, a big part of why I love it is the location--right at the BART station, and 5 blocks from our HQ. But it's also because they really go out of their way to take care of their guests.On my most recent stay, my day had gotten off to an awful start. Woke up to find my flight to SF cancelled, and I had to be there for an annual departmental meeting at noon. I arranged a replacement flight, but my cab no-showed, and I missed it. Another taxi to another airport, bad traffic, not enough time to check in; but I managed somehow, only to end up in the very back row next to a woman with a coughing brat in her lap. I got to the Palomar at 11:15am. I stopped in, figuring I'd at least drop my bag and use a men's room. The clerk at the front desk asked how she could help me, so I asked if it were possible to check in, explaining that I knew it was very early, etc. While she was checking, she asked how my morning was going--so I told her the story. Well the room they had set aside for me wasn't ready, so she upgraded me. And I had half an hour to relax in a deluxe room before going to the meeting. Now I hadn't been to the hotel in over a year, and I had booked my room on their website at the cheapest special rate they offer all year. But I was able to go to my meeting in a good frame of mind because the Palomar took care of me. Will I stay there again? You beat--every time I can get a rate that won't alarm our auditors.

<Author>TheWinston
<Content>Overpriced Just stayed at the hotel March 14-15. The beds were extremely comfortable and provided a great night's sleep. The location is also a huge plus....close to the cable car and right next to bus/street car stops and lots of dining nearby. However, the hotel definately does not have the 'luxury' feel, though you may pay a luxury price for it. The rooms were small and the bathrooms were tiny. We had a view of market street which was great, though they originally tried sticking us in on the interior of the building, facing the roof, so we called the front desk to get into the other room. And keep in mind, if you reserve online, don't expect them to uphold any special requests you may make. We requested a room on the highest floor possible, yet we were given a room on the 5th floor (the lowest floor in the hotel.) Our second room was on the 6th floor and given to us 10 min after check-in, so they obviously had rooms available on higher levels. All the staff was very friendly and usually helpful. The 'business center' had computers with internet connections, though know in advance that the internet there costs extra, which should not be the case for the price you pay for a night's stay. The parking was $42 a day with valet, which is comparable to other hotels in the area. All in all it was a 'nice' hotel, but the price does not reflect what you get in return.

<Author>Fernleigh1
<Content>New decor makes a difference We spent 5 nights there at the end of February -- Wednesday thru Monday. It must have been our 4th or 5th visit to the Palomar.The hotel is nearing completion of a substantial remodeling of the sleeping rooms. The previous zebra motif has given way to soft modern colors and lines. The rooms seem both calmer and larger than previously, but also more luxurious. Only complaint is that the desk chairs were not really desk chairs, and more stylish than useful when being used for that work thing. The bathrooms also seem to have been refurbished, and a new range of toiletries is on display.Overall, it was an excellent experience. Staff are a little impersonal, with a somewhat forced welcome back when you come through the door. But, they did what was requested, and everything worked just fine. Out the front door and around the side is the entrance to the Bloomingdales in the expanded Westfields center. Diagnoally across the street is the Metreon theater complex. Across the street is the Marriott.So, the location is quite good, the hotel is quiet and upscale. Staff do their jobs. It was a good thing. We'll definitely use the Palomar again. Like so many of the Kimpton properties, it's a classy but affordable act.

<Author>LawyerBoyNYC
<Content>Unfortunately not that great I REALLY wanted to love this hotel. The website made it look great and the reviews I had read were very positive. However, despite the reasonable room rates (I paid 179/night), this is just not a hotel I would return to.GENERAL: The problem with Kimpton hotels, in my opinion, is that they are theme hotels rather than true luxury hotels. The theme of the Palomar is fancy hotel. It emulates luxury, but doesn't actually achieve it.LOCATION: The hotel is located very centrally on the corner of Market Street and 4th St. The particular street corner is ridden with somewhat sleazy types, and the building abuts an Old Navy store.LOBBY: I generally enjoy large, open spaces, and the lobby, though well-appointed, was the opposite.ROOMS: TINY!!!!! The very friendly receptionist had even upgraded me to one of the larger rooms, and that was still an extremely small room. The room was nicely appointed but, again, TINY!! The bathroom was so tiny that, sitting on the toilet, my knees nearly touched the cheaply painted-over sliding door that separates the bedroom from the bathroom. The bedding was awful. The pillows were tiny and not firm enough.SERVICE: This is the hotel's one big plus. Everyone from the receptionist to Virgil, the very friendly and knowledgeable concierge, to the bellboys, were professional and courteous.RESTAURANT: The restaurant, Fifth Floor, has received rave reviews on Zagat and elsewhere. It bills itself as a gourmet fine dining restaurant with a star chef. I have eaten in some of the finest restaurants domestically and internationally, and this restaurant just wasn't that great. The service was terrific, but the food, though flavorful and inventive, wasn't worth the $173 price tag (for one person!!). Entrees priced between 40-52 dollars!!!SUMMARY: If you are in dire need of a boutique hotel in San Francisco, go to the W. It's near the Palomar, but it is a first-rate version of itself rather than a second-rate version of another hotel (which is what, sadly, most of the Kimpton hotels are).

<Author>travelmum
<Content>Lovely hotel, huge room First, I don't understand the comments about the rooms being small. I booked the cheapest room, and it was huge! I just presumed all the rooms were that size. I asked for a quiet room, and didn't want one overlooking the street, as I guessed that would be noisy, and also wanted a non-smoking room (I think the whole hotel is non-smoking, but I didn't want a room that someone had smoked in). We were given a room at the back of the hotel, with apologies that it overlooked offices, as that was the quietest. The room was super quiet, once the door was shut we couldn't hear a thing. It was a huge room though. We didn't really watch tv, but if someone did, they might find the tv too far away from the beds, especially for watching a movie. We kind of felt that a lot of the room space was wasted, but it was certainly a large room. The bathroom also was huge. Lovely fittings in the bathroom, and we liked the 'arty' touch throughout the hotel.The location was great. I purposefully wanted something not right on Union Square, as that sounded noisy. I liked this location just south of the square, as it was easy to get to for transportation, stores, a grocery store down the road. We walked everywhere from the hotel. We're good walkers, but still we walked up hills, over to China Town and on to North Beach, across to Nob Hill, and took public transportation to the Haight, etc.No coffee maker in the rooms, but excellent organic coffee in the lobby, so I'd just go down there each morning and bring some up. Free internet access in the room was handy. Also, various newspapers available on each floor or outside your room. I liked the smaller size of the hotel and would definitely return.

<Author>youcanon
<Content>Location, Location, Location! After reading multiple reviews online (mainly this website) I booked a room for our family of four at the Palomar. We were a family of four with two older teenagers, and I was looking for something that would accomodate varying personalities. My husband is older, hates shopping, favors museums. My daughter wanted to SHOP, SHOP, SHOP! Our son would probably have preferred to have been left home, and I just wanted everyone to be happy. The Palomar seemed tucked back from the traffic on the main road, but it was within easy walking distance of several museums and LOADS of shopping. Chinatown was also within easy walking distance. The staff at the Palomar was SO courteous--always greeting us with a smile, opening doors (It may have helped to have the attractive 20 year old daughter along.) The room was not large, but luxuriously appointed with down comforters, really nice sheets and towels. I thought at one point that I should have booked TWO rooms, but we weren't IN the room that much, and we really didn't mind the rare family closeness. As a matter of fact, when we look back on the trip more than a year later, we talk about the night we stayed in and ordered a movie on the television as one of our favorite times on the trip.  We booked one of those tours to Alcatraz, Muir Woods, Sauselito, and the bus stopped right in front of the hotel and picked us up the morning we were going to Muir Woods. We found the location perfect for our needs. My husband and I would wake up early and head out for one of the Starbucks within easy walking distance. The location was wonderful, the room VERY nice, the staff extre mely courteous and helpful. I would definitely stay there again.

I was not interested in staying in a monster size hotel only to feel like just a room number. I was also presented with a gift, a Palomar tote bag. This was unexpected and very thoughtful.I booked the room through the hotel's website and they fulfilled my special requests. The room was clean and I approved of the decor. The ceilings were at least 10 feet high, which is a nice touch. All it all, it was perfect. I left for dinner and when I returned, the little trash that I generated was already removed from the room, new towels were provided, and robes laid out on the bed. Check out was just as easy. I was more than pleased with the high level of service and condition of the hotel. I look forward to staying at this hotel again, hopefully sooner than later.

<Author>jenncLJ
<Content>Great City Hotel Experience! I wasn't quite sure what to expect from this hotel, as I had never even heard of it before. My friend booked this hotel for us on a recent stay, and I have to say that I was pleasantly surprised. From the moment we walked into the chic, hip lobby, I was struck by how kind and courteous the desk staff was. The atmosphere is upscale and hip, it would appeal to anyone who demands the best in service and style, for the business or pleasure travelers alike.The room was very clean and spacious, with fabulous leopard patterned carpet and some wonderful Aveda toiletries waiting for us in the attractively decorated bathroom. Everything was in good working order in the room, and the bed was extremely comfortable. The bellhop brought up our things very quickly and our every request was met in a timely and courteous manner.My favorite part of this hotel was the amazing mini dinner that we had in the Fifth Floor Restaurant. The restaurant was full with holiday party goers and other guests, and we didn't have a reservation. However, the hostess accomodated us with no questions asked and we were seated as soon as we got into the crowded room. I had the chicory salad and sour dough encrusted mackeral, both of which were outstanding, well-prepared, tasty, and beautifully presented. The service in the restaurant was as impeccable as it was at the front desk/room attendants, courteous, prompt and professional. This is some of the best food I have ever had the pleasure of eating in a hotel restaurant.Overall, this hotel is a real find in the City, for its upscale and low-key elegance, wonderful cuisine, and super service. I would come back for the service alone. All the staff, from the valet to the front desk, was deferential and more than happy to accomodate our every wish. This hotel is fairly new, but I'm sure that it will become a SF landmark in the years to come. If you want a wonderful, city chic hotel experience, this one is for you! Happy Staying!

<Author>nsvlbimmerguy
<Content>A nice property We stayed at the Palomar for quite a while, 9 nights while attending a conference in the city. Access to the hotel via the BART system from the bay airports is easy as there's a stop across the street. Check-in was fast and pleasant, the lobby small, but well turned out.Our room was was nicely appointed. Though, while artfully done, the finishes, textiles and carpet all looked a little tired and in need of a touch up. One annoyance was the lack of a proper dresser or bureau the only piece of storage furniture being the TV armoire which also housed the mini bar, books, etc. The bathroom was just ok.A couple annoyances, while access to public transport is nice, there is a prominent stop right in front of the hotel so quite often during the day the sidewalk is packed with people waiting for the bus, also the housekeeping service started out ok, but slowly became more inconsistent as the week unfolded.The front desk staff were very helpful, attentive and able to answer most questions I had about the city, etc.Free WiFi, a pay option at most hotels of comparable quality in the area, was nice as well.This is a great location for shopping in Union Square and area restaurants, etc.Also, this is the quietest hotel I've ever stayed at in SF, particularly with having a 6th floor room on Market St.I would probably stay again, though only for less than the $219 reserved through the hotel website.

<Author>VCRtraveler
<Content>Over Priced, Lacking Customer Service We recently returned from a distressing stay at the Palomar. We were so excited to be staying there because of their reputation for customer service and the positive reviews. We booked over the hotel's central reservation line. They gave us a rate which was pricey, but included parking and breakfast. When we checked in they said that I was mistaken and that only parking was included. I tried to clear this up but was told there was no manager on duty and to call the central reservation line (they confrimed a note on my file on their computer system, that my understanding was correct but said they could do nothing to help me, and that I would have to sort it out at the hotel.) So, no one was available either at the hotel or central reservations to help sort this out.In the end, I wrote a note for the day manager. She was unavailable in the morning, but then left a voice message in my room saying that I was wrong. When I talked to her in person, and asked her to check the file, she found that there was indeed a note saying that the breakfast AND parking were included. If anyone at the front desk had bothered to check the notes on the computer reservation, they would have seen this (they refused to do this). However, it was too late, by the time it was sorted out it was well past breakfast. In the end, they offered a discount on a room service charge for the previous night. But, it did not save the siutation. I felt very disrespectfully treated, and ended up in tears. The customer service put a real pall on our stay, and I ended up spending a couple of hours of our precious vacation time trying to get them to honor the commitment their own reservation department had made. Very disappointing. A discount on a room service charge in no way made up for the disrespectful treatment, or their own lack of coordination between the hotel and their own reservations department.Overall: The other staff (concierge, bell and wait staff) were very friendly and helpful. The frontdesk and management were not helpful at all. The hotel itself is unique, but worn around the edges. They allow pets, and there was dog hair on the ottoman in our room.The location is very nice. The view from our room was to an internal courtyard that faced other rooms, we could not open the window to our room. The restaurant for dinner had organic local foods and was wonderful. I agree with the previous reviewer...the pocket bathroom doors to the small rooms allow no privacy.Overall, I was so disappointed with the customer service and rudeness. I would not recommend that anyone stay here. It is a decent property, but when things like this happen and there is no commitment to correcting misunderstandings it makes the whole experience upsetting. Paying this amount of money for a room, we expect far better customer service. Also, we expect that what the promises of the central reservation department will be honored, and not argued about at the front desk. For the price, there are better hotels with better customer service.

<Author>SYV
<Content>Wonderful hotel, wonderful staff! Since it was our first visit to San Francisco, we decided it would be fun to stay at two different hotels. We chose the Palomar and Harbor Court hotels, and according to TripAdvisor, they were similar in traveler satisfaction. That was certainly not our experience, and we wished we had stayed at the Palomar the entire trip.The Palomar has the best staff of any hotel we have ever visited. Everyone, from the bell desk to concierge was friendly, professional, and knowledgable. I booked a Executive King through the hotel's website and when we checked in we had been upgraded to Room 816, which was a beautiful room with large windows that overlooked the street. I was concerned at first that the noise from the street would be bothersome but it wasn't. At night we didn't hear anything and slept great. The bathroom was very nice, with thoughtful amenities like a magnifying makeup mirror and ample room to put personal belongings. The room was very comfortable and the decor was beautiful, but also fun, with leopard print carpeting. The bed was very comfortable with high quality bed linens. There were four bed pillows, something we really appreciated. A pretty room means nothing to us, though, if the hotel staff isn't what it should be. The staff is great, we felt welcome and pampered from the minute we walked in. I used the concierge (Yeme) several times and she gave us great advice and was so very nice. We also asked directions several times and the bell desk was helpful and accurate.The location is great, and we didn't rent a car while we were there. We walked everywhere, or took public transportation which is easily accessible. A couple of tips that are very important - if you plan to visit Alcatraz, be sure to buy your tickets through blueandgoldfleet[]ahead of time. There were many people trying to get tickets and they couldn't - sold out. Also, if you want to take a wine tour and plan to use a tour company or limo, it would be best to choose the company ahead of time and make reservations. The company we wanted to use (recommended by Yeme) was sold out for the weekend, so we had to go with someone else. It was ok, glad we did it, but the other would have been better. Best meal we had was at Scomas, on Pier 47. Great seafood!We were so pleased with this hotel that we will definately come back to it next time we go to San Francisco, which I hope will be soon. It is a beautiful, wonderful place!

<Author>mbgirl06
<Content>Great Stay at the Hotel Palomar My boyfriend and I just got back from a two night stay at the Hotel Palomar. This was my first trip to San Francisco and I chose this hotel based on previous reviews. I have to say thank you to all of you who posted your reviews on this hotel because they were right on. This hotel was great. Here are some tips of advice for those of you who are considering this hotel for your stay in San Francisco:I used the advice from a previous review on the parking structure at 5th and Mission and it worked out great. It was only a block from the hotel and half the price ($23 a day) of what it would have been to park at the hotel. For those of you who want to shop, this is the perfect location. Every store you can think of is within walking distance. But, be prepared for the ever changing climate. Although it was very sunny both days, it can be very deceiving. Make sure and bring light sweaters or jackets and comfortable shoes. Cabs can be a little pricey, so be prepared to do a lot of walking. We took the trolley once down to Fisherman's Wharf and that was enough for me. We had to wait for about 25 minutes to get on at Powell and Market St and unless you get a seat, you'll be holding on for dear life. It was fun for the experience though.If you do go to Fisherman's Wharf, I highly recommend Chic's Seafood restaurant. It is on the second level on Pier 39. Our meal was fantastic and reasonably priced. As for the hotel itself: We had a king bed room. It was a bit small, but all we did was sleep there so it didn't matter to us. Our room also did not have a dresser, but for two nights it wasn't a bid deal. Also no coffee maker in the room, but it forced us to get up and out of bed to get fresh coffee in the lobby. Our bed was incredibly comfortable which made up for the compact size. Our room was always very clean and stocked up with fresh towels and Aveda products every day. They even had turn down service which added a nice touch. Even though the hotel is in a busy area, our room faced the courtyard, so we didn't hear any street noise at night. The hotel staff are all very friendly and accomodating.Overall, this was a fantastic trip and a great stay at the Hotel Palomar. I would definitely recommend this hotel.

<Author>ZaiZaiLv
<Content>Great Stay @ Palomar Palomar is a small boutique hotel, part of Kimpton Hotels located on Market and Fourth St. The hotel itself is not that big, it's only 9 stories high, however, it was very homey and inviting. Positives:- Location is perfect, a few blocks away from Union Square, less than a block away from Sony Metreon and San Francisco Shopping Center. - We are big on Customer Service, so that is the first thing that we noticed when we arrived. Everyone was friendly and very approachable. They always greeted us with a big smile and was willing to help. - During our check in, we were upgraded to a Suite without even asking. Perhaps because we are members of the Kimpton? They also greeted us with a welcome bag which consisted of a bottle of distiled water and an apple. It's not a big thing, but it's a nice gesture.- We have stayed at many different hotels in San Francisco, but we have never encountered hotel rooms so quiet before. We were on the 8th floor and we could not hear the busy streets at all. We were expecting to hear a lot of noises, (I even had my earplugs ready) so this was a nice surprise. Some of the problems we encountered during our stay:- I usually don't use shampoo and conditioners provided by Hotels, but Kimpton usually provides great amentines, so I decided not to bother to bring my own. The shampoo (Aveda) really dried up my hair. Not a big deal really, for I was smacked in the middle of downtown, an easy walk to get my regular shampoo. - The pillows were small. We are used to having either queen/king size pillows on a king size bed, but these pillows provided were the standard pillows. They were so small that they looked out of place on such a large bed.- The bathroom was nice, and the tub was big enough, however, the water in the tub took forever to drain. In fact, the water reached my ankle when I was taking a shower. We let the hotel know about this, but we were encountering the same problems the whole time we were there. The toilet wasn't flushing properly also. We had to flush at least twice or three times each time. Overall, we had a great stay at Palomar, and most likely will return.

<Author>Ridgesas
<Content>A Gem in San Fran! We found this hotel by chance via Expedia and booked it give the positive reviews on TA. This hotel is a great outique?style property situated right in the heart of San Fran. All the places we wanted to see were easily accessible from this hotel either by walking or by tram/train/streetcar/bus all of which are within a block of this hotel. Outside the hotel you will find pan handlers and homeless people however, this is to be expected anywhere in San Fran (you can also expect this outside the Four Season which is only a block away).The property is very clean and stylish without being too over the top. The room was on the smaller side but very clean and comfortable. The bed was great along with the linens and towels.We rented a car and took a day trip to Napa which is highly recommended. The wineries were great and the food was amazing.Being the 4th of July, we expected warm weather and were somewhat surprised at how cold it is in San Fran. The weather reports said the temperature would be around 20 but with the wind/fog it was more like 10. Other than the cold weather we enjoyed this hotel and would definitely stay here again.

My apologies to the wonderful staff for my poor memory with their names. I do remember that some of them had name tags that also included an artist name of their choice. <Author>JoGustoSantaCruz
<Content>You'll probably enjoy this hotel! This hotel is right above the Old Navy store on Market street, just blocks from Union Square shopping, and one short block from the Sony Metreon.The staff was helpful and friendly. We were able to arrange in-room massages via the concierge, no problem. <Author>hairykid
<Content>An Absolute Gem The Palomar is simply one of the most comfortable, cosy hotels that I have ever experienced, and I travel a lot for business. I usually stick to the large chain hotels because you can rely on consistency, but I was so happy to have chosen the Palomar for my last trip. My double room ($259 per night) was vast (love the leopard print carpet), with a good-sized bathroom. Although only steps away from Market Street, there was no noise to disturb my sleep in the huge bed. When I arrived in my room, the TV was playing soft music and calming pictures of waterfalls - just what I needed after a gruelling 10-hour flight from London. All the fixtures were stylish and clean, with thick robes in the closet and chocolate every night on the pillow.I would definitely stay here again as a tourist, my only negative points are as a business traveller. Room service breakfast does not start for hot food until 7 am weekdays/8 am weekends. While this is fine for tourists, for those of us who have 8 am Sunday meetings it's not ideal. I found the room service food to be the only aspect of my stay which let the place down - dinner on my first night was really disappointing. Expensive and badly cooked. The room service food does not come from the restaurant kitchen, and it shows. Also, there is no business centre in the hotel, although it is possible to send faxes from the front desk. There is no coffee machine in the room either, another negative for the seriously jet-lagged.But these points did not make me regret not staying in the Marriott across the road. I'm not used to the kind of personal attention that you get at the Palomar, and it was a very nice change.

<Author>cbfnyc
<Content>Always a pleasure Recently stayed at the Palomar Hotel during a weekend birthday celebration. The front desk staff is exceedingly pleasant and thoughtful and they make every effort to make the check procedure as fast and easy as possible.The room is well appointed, with every amenity. The beds are comfy, the sheets soft and everything is spotless. They offer free wireless internet, which lots of hotels charge $10/day extra for.The exceptional thing that happened is that I had mentioned being in town for my birthday. About an hour after checking in, there was a gentleman at the door with a complimentary half bottle of wine and a box of truffles from their restaurant, The Fifth Floor. It was so wonderful and thoughtful and truly made the day special.In terms of location, you can't do much better in San Francisco. It's a two block walk to Union Square, all the shopping is in close proximity, and there is a BART station a half block away. There are many hotels in this area, and I have stayed at a few others, but for a total package in terms of price, location, amenities and service, would definitely give the Palomar top marks.

<Author>PaintTheCity
<Content>Absolutely Positive Stay at the Palomar The location of the Palomar is perfect for stepping out any time of the day or night - you're less than 2 blocks from Union Square, lots of shopping, restaurants and people. The Ferry Market is a 15 minute walk, highly recommended - and if you don't want to walk anymore, public transportation, cable cars and taxis are literally a step away. Ultimately, the staff makes a stay at a hotel matter - and they were all above and beyond my expectations. The hotel partners with a limo service that was fantastic - which is another great suggestion in touring the city and beyond. Money well spent. The doormen will arrange the service for you.I booked a king and upgraded to a suite on the 9th floor - which was divine. If you need the room to spread out and enjoy the view, do it. And after walking all over the city all day, the jacuzzi tub and the shower take away all your aches and pains. And if you don't have the energy to get back out for dinner, or you want a good breakfast to start off the day right - the restaurant's food is great. A little on the high-end price wise, but it's convenient. The bed was wonderful, the room service was great and it was quiet and peaceful when I retired for the night. There wasn't one single negative thing to report about the Hotel Palomar. I will always choose this hotel in future visits to San Francisco.

<Author>ShannonHB
<Content>Great Hotel! I stayed in the Hotel Palomar over President's Day weekend, and it was a lovely hotel! The rooms were quiet and meticulously clean, spacious (a rare find in San Francisco), and well appointed, with a very comfortable bed. The staff members were gracious, helpful and polite, and were very accommodating when we arrived at a late hour. In addition, the location is desirable and close to BART, which was very convenient for travel. Overall, a very tasteful, sophisticated, private hotel.The only qualities of which I would take note, not bad but are definitely a matter of preference:1) Pet friendly, which is fine, except for the incessantly barking dog across the hallway. However, management handled the problem promptly. 2) Very quiet, and guests keep to themselves. In other words, if you are looking for a lively spot rather than a private getaway, may not be the best place.3) The bar is not open on Sunday evenings, and service is a bit slow.4) The concierge was not terribly knowledgeable. So, if you are not familiar with a city, and are relying on the concierge for suggestions, you might consider doing your research prior to arriving.

<Author>voll002
<Content>Nice people, nice hotel Reading the last review, I feel obligated to post my recent experience at the Hotel Palomar. Maybe I'm not quite as picky as other people, but I found the customer service at the hotel to be excellent, as compared to the 200+ other hotels I've stayed at in the last 12 months. Apparently the hotel was good enough to win the Conde Nast Traveler's 2005 Gold List of World's Best Places to stay, so I guess I'm not alone in thinking that it's a nice place to stay.Being a road warrior, I'm also an Inner Circle Elite Member, so it's possible I get treated a little better than the average customer, but compared with my treatment at other chains (Intercontinental, Marriott, Starwood), I found the customer service to be more than adequate.Checkin:I arrived early at the hotel (approx 1 PM), and didn't expect to be given a room, but the desk clerk found one for me without a problem. Based on my Inner Circle status, I asked if I could get upgraded. Again, based on past experiences with equal status at other chains, I was more than prepared to accept a negative response. The desk clerk upgraded me to a jacuzzi suite, no extra charge. She was very friendly, smiling, and welcoming, traits that I unfortunately see a paucity of in the hotel business.Room Service: I believe that room service at most Kimpton hotels is not quite at the same level as larger hotels, because they are boutique hotels, which are smaller in scale by definition than main chain hotels. That said, I think the quality of food I've ordered at Kimptons hotels exceeds their rivals.I did have breakfast at the hotel restaurant, and though expensive, it really was not any more than rival hotels (esp. for San Francisco). Service was fast and good, so no problems there.Room: Clean, with relatively new appearing furniture (again, maybe I'm just not as picky as others - but I do stay in enough hotels to be able to judge quality of room accomodations). The bathroom had a jacuzzi with separate walk-in shower with Aveda toiletries.Overall: Considering I booked the room with a Travelzoo discount of 150 (with $25 discount towards restaurant meal), I would most definitely stay there again. And the friendly, welcoming staff was the icing on the top which is the feature that would lead me to stay there again.I think that the same Travelzoo offer also has free parking for those driving, and may be running through March (on the weekend). They also have Hot Date Hot Rate specials (like all Kimptons)

<Content>Service as it Should Be The Palomar is a striking hotel. Everything is subtle and refined and very comfortable. You know you have arrived somewhere special from the moment you walk in. <Author>Lanea
<Content>Great Service  We had planned an 8 day trip to explore SF and chose the Palomar largely due to the high rating on Trip Advisor. I had requested a high floor and a city view. We ended up with a fairfly high floor but no city view probably due to my travel agent (Liberty Travel) stinking. We had a non descript view but it was super quiet which ended up being fine since there was plenty of noise in the city when we went out. I have nothing to compare this to in SF so please keep that in mind. The room (deluxe king) was small but nicely arranged. Use their luggage rack as there is not enough drawer space but who really cares. The bathroom does have that sliding door but it ended being fine. The bed was super comfortable although the TV reception was lousy due to neaby construction. The concierges there are great. Super friendly and helpful. The whole staff really makes you feel like you are the only ones in the hotel (wait.. were we?). Actually there was a big Intel convention down the street so I think the hotel was fairly crowded.The hotel is a couple o' blocks below all the major shopping in Union Square which is fine. We are natural food eaters so we lucked out that there was a Whole Foods about a 10 minute walk South. No problem since too much room service gets expensive. They give you free use of Yoga equipment for use in your room or, as in our case, for use in the numerous SF yoga studios. Plenty of nearby great food and every recommendation we received from the concierges were spot on. If you want to catch a movie you will be one block from the largest Loews? multiplex ever created. A million screens. Housekeeping was quite excellent. I was worried when I read a less than stellar review just before we left but our experience was in line with our fairly high expectations. Clean, great service, great location.. Enjoy..

<Author>Likes_to_eat
<Content>Tips if you stay at the Palomar First of all, the Palomar is at a great location. Lots of great shopping around, the Metreon for a late movie, the SOMA (best brownies at their cafte), and right on the cable car line.1) Best hotel rate can be found on their web site. We did the great rates deal for $139/nite plus taxes.2) Request a handicap room, if available at check-in. These are larger rooms. They will fill your request if no one reserves them. Otherwise, a room with a view to the zen court is quite nice and very quiet. 3) Hotel parking is $42 + taxes with in/out priviledges, but if you park down the street at the Metreon public parking lot, it's $22/24 hours with NO in/out priviledges. But in SF, you won't need your car! Everything is accessible by foot, cab, cable car or bus. By the way, the $11/1 day pass for the cable car/metro is worth it. But start early, as the cable car line is always long. The cable car start/ticket booth is across the street from the Palomar.btw, the hotel has a very good driving map of the city showing the one-way streets direction. Very helpful if you're driving down there.4) If you're driving in the city, you will need a car to get to the Golden Gate bridge view site, so do this first thing when you're driving into the city. Parking is $5/all day at the view site, so I suggest everyone do what we did - pass your all-day parking pass (which you put in your windshield) on to someone else when you're getting ready to leave the parking lot! Some jerk sold me his for half-price (cheap *******!), but you should just pass it on. It's an all-day pass, so everyone should be able to make use of it!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good Hotel but nothing to get excited about This is a good solid boutique hotel where you will have a comfortable stay. There is no wow factor - so if you are looking for spectacular views or grand lobbies, this is not the place. The location is good - about a block from Union Square. The rooms are decent sized - we had a executive king on the 6th floor. At first they gave us a similar room on the seventh flr which was facing a wall - terrible view. But upon request, they gave us the one on the 6th flr with a view of market street - much better.The bed, pillows, linens are all very high quality and comfortable. Service was for Room Service (good food!), Valet parking and Housekeeping.The doubleglazed windows really do block the street noise out.We could however hear the street musicians everyday on market street right below our room. They stop before 10:00 pm. And the music was actually very good and added to the general atmosphere. The lobby is very nondescript, and breakfast was blah.

<Author>Great_NW_Traveler
<Content>A total class-act; nicest place I've stayed This was a superb location and the accommodations were first-class all the way. We booked through Priceline packages and had requested early check-in and late check-out. They were most accommodating. Although the parking was steep ($42 with tax for valet parking in/out privileges) it was worth it. We used the in/out privileges several times each day and received superior service each time. The hotel is elegant, well-appointed and the very best thing is that there is absolutely no street noise of any kind, which is incredible considering the location. We had a fifth floor room that was closest to the lounge and there was some localized noise from that, but I popped my earplugs in and never had another issue. My hubby wasn't bothered in the slightest. Maid service was beyond reproach and occurred twice daily with evening bed turndown. The restaurant was fine - we had brunch there one day; never seemed busy and it was costly. I am glad for an option to eat there, but it wasn't anything special. Without question, this was the nicest hotel I've ever stayed at and I'd recommend this to anyone; I hope to be able to stay there again.

A perfect get away at an intimate hotel. We will definitely return!

<Author>SCFCanton
<Content>Very Nice Stay My wife and I went to San Francisco  Napa for our 10th anniversary. We stayed at the Palomar at the back end of our trip - and it was well worth it. The staff made us feel special and took really good care of us. We only stayed two nights, but their hospitality made us feel like we were long-time friends and frequent guests. The bell staff was very efficient and they brought up our bags right away. When we were getting ready to leave for the airport, they helped us box up and seal a case of wine we were checking as luggage on our flight. For our anniversary they gave us a nice bottle of red and box of chocolates. They also obtained great dinner reservations for us. Our room was really nice and spacious. Turn down service was a nice touch - they left more chocolates. My wife loved the bath accessories, hair-dryer, etc. I really liked having the nice stereo, etc. in the enterainment cabinet. It was nice to listen to music on a decent sound system in your room. The hotel is in a great location if you going to use Market Street as your home base for your San Francisco stay. Palomar is close to the Pier/Wharf areas, the Financial District and the chain shopping (Macy's Nordstrom, etc.) We booked using a online special rate that included a parking credit - but most of the rental car agencies have return counters close to the hotel. Thus we could have returned our rental car two days earlier and used the parking credit for credit at the Fifth Floor restaurant (one of SF's best.) If we had any complaints, its that the staff did not always give us the best or clearest directions to the various sites/restaurants that we were going to visit. The directions were mostly vague ... walk up 4th three blocks, turn right - its on that street kind of thing. Because of that it took us 10-15 minutes to find the hotel, find one of our restaurants, etc. We liked the overall look and feel of the hotel, the location, and our stay. For the price we expected a good experience and we got it.

<Author>dwldds
<Content>Swanky hotel at a great price I went to San Francisco on business and found the Palomar after unsuccessfully booking at the Marriott across the way. This was my first experience at a boutique hotel. The main thing that attracted me to this hotel was the modern style and attention to detail without the expensive room rates. When I arrived, I was not disappointed. The lobby, though small was minimalistically classy. There was something different about this place.....The check in was fine, and the front desk staff were quite friendly.My room was wonderful. Lots of characteristic swank, very modern, sharp and clean. I was impressed with the CD/radio, the decor, and the AVEDA toilettries which all indicate Kimpton's desire to offer high quality affordably. I had a bit of trouble during my stay - a false alarm and a premature check-out botch. However, The staff were quite apologetic and did what they could to accommodate me. I was moved to a different room and discovered that the decor was essentially the same from room to room. Not surprising, but probably the secret to allowing them to offer what they do. The hotel has a restaurant/lounge that - as it turns out - is frequented by locals moreso than hotel guests (at least so I think). This would be fine, but the fact that the lounge was located on a floor adjacent to guest rooms makes me wonder if this was the wisest form of planning. Still, the noise level rises only around happy hour and is not otherwise a problem. The fitness room is compact but the essentials are there. Business types may frequent this hotel, and this is why I found the fitness room to be used very rarely by hotel guests. The novelty of the hotel may wear off, since it's a lot of surface wow and not too much depth in amenities. But this is not a resort, and as far as hotels go, this is a winner if you match style and class with the manageable room rates.
