<Author>thoggy
<Content>Here's the good and bad about the Palomar... My girlfriend and I visited San Francisco for 4 nights and after looking around online a lot, we chose to stay at the Hotel Palomar. Here's my thoughts on it:- Once you have done your looking around online and found what you think is the best deal, go to the Palomar website and see what they are charging for the exact same type o room. If you call the number for reservations or go to the Kimpton Group website you can see they have a best rate guaranteed deal where they match the rate you found plus you get late checkout times and a room upgrade if available. The room upgrade is probably a little iffy according to other reviews on this site, but it did work for us. We booked a King Deluxe (their base room) and were upgraded to a Executive King room which is slightly larger and faces out rather than looking at the inner courtyard. The room is still not overly large (350 square feet) but the view was nice (Market Street, with Macy's etc. in view). I should mention that I wrote an email to the reservations people at the hotel asking for a room upgrade as well so not sure if the upgrade happened as a resut of the Kimpton guarantee or my email. Still, well worth a try. We got ours for $200 U.S. a night including all taxes which while not a huge steal was decent.- Hotel location is pretty decent, located right in the middle of the shopping district and centrally located for any touristy things you are plannin on doing. The one thing I would say is that while the immediate neighbourhood is good, SF has a big problem with homeless people and you will often see them in front of the hotel. This is true everyhere in the downtown area so not a big deal but still a little unsettling. It was always relieving to have the doormen open the oor for you as you approach and escape into the lobby.- Service was fine for us, though we didn't ask for very much. We checked in late in the evening with no problem and the bellhop was very friendly and informative. The desk staff were polite but never seemed to go out of their way to say hello as you walk by or anything. Maids were friendly and said hi and smiled whenever they saw you.- Design and decor was great. It is a beautiful hotel if you are into modern style and some nice luxury touches. There was nothing in our room that turned me off the place. I hate when you stay at a hotel and it seems nice but then you notice scuff marks on the wall or cracks in the bathroom tiles and so on. The king bed was super comfortable though if you or your partner are a restless sleeper it might be problematic as it was somewhat springy and when my girlfriend would turn over, I would bounce a little on my side. That said, it was a great sleep with wonderful linens and pillows. One of the best beds I have slept in, in a hotel. The TV was fine and the Sony CD player was very nice with some music and a light jazz station coming in very clearly. The bathroom does lack a little bit in privacy as it is a sliding door that does not latch or close. It is not see through or anything but when the bed is right beside the bathroom door you may hear more noises when someone uses it then you would prefer. If you aren't shy though, no problem!- Overall it was a pretty good experience. If we returned to San Francisco I would probably stay there again, though I would be tempted to stay in a different part of the city. We were there on vacation and it proved a decent home base from which to go out each day. Hope you found this useful as I know reading the reviews helped me decide!  
<Date>May 30, 2005

<Content>Fantastic Hotel This hotel made my boyfriend and I feel like superstars. They were incredibly attentive from the moment we arrived....even allowing us to check in to our room 3 hours early. Upon check out the hotel arranged for a luxury town car to take us to the airport. We were extremely impressed by the service and location of this hotel. It is right in the center of everything: shopping, dining, tourism. I would definitely recommend this hotel to anyone who is visiting the San Fran area.

<Author>rosebud
<Content>First class all the way My wife and I loved our 4 night stay at the Hotel Palomar. They honored my request for an exterior facing room, higher floor. Limited views of Market Street and nearby tall buildings/Marriott. Very spacious room, great layout and calming interior design with in room CD and all the tech equipment you could want. Phenomenal service, great location between Soma and Union Square shopping, a stone's throw from the Moscone Convention Center, half a short block from the Bart Station. We ate at the hotel's posh five star restaurant, The Fifth Floor, which was a splurge but worth every penny for a memorable evening of out of this world cuisine, romantic atmosphere and doting service (the much more affordable breakfast was also very good, with quick and convenient service). A great home base in a world class city.

<Author>lass=
<Content>Great room, not-so-great service I was scheduled to be here for a convention for four nights. When I arrived, they told me that they were full because another party had decided unexpectedly to extend their stay, and so they booked me and about ten other convention attendees at another hotel. Though I thought the lack of a room was inexcusable, the situation was handled reasonably well by the front desk staff. However, when I went back the next day for my room at noon (they had said I would be scheduled for an earlier arrival), the Palomar told me that my room was still being cleaned and to come back in a half-hour. Three hours later, at 3:00 pm, I was again told to come back in a half-hour for my room. Finally, at about 5:00 pm, I was given a room key. The room itself was smallish but very nice. Sleek, yet attractive and comfortable. Great amenities, including some cool CD samplers. Very nice bathroom, though the tub grout could use a good cleaning. They upgraded me to a room with a nice exterior view and sent a bottle of wine for my troubles, plus coupons for free breakfast every day. But I had to push for those.The restaurant is intended primarily for dinner. They'll serve you breakfast, but only grudgingly -- the waitresses in the morning have tons of attitude and were very cold.

<Author>ATourist2day
<Content>nice and different The Palomar is not what we expected. It is very modern and has an understated European luxury feel to it. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>We loved it! Great location, great staff, great decor. Shower pressure could be better. It's true, it is a hassle to have to go downstairs to grab coffee. We were pretty surprised by this too, but we really didn't mind much. It was actually kind of nice to get out and stretch our legs in the morning.The staff is incredibly friendly, helpful, prompt, and polite. They had good recommendations, and were very accomodating with any requests.We didn't get a chance to try the restaurant.We stayed in a Deluxe King room on the 5th floor for an average of $167 per night. Not bad for the days around New Year's Eve. No street noise, great decor, big room. CD player and free newspaper in the morning were nice touches.My biggest complaint was the water pressure in the shower. It may have just been our room, but it should have had a lot more water pressure. Otherwise the bathroom was comfortable and clean. Really didn't like the Aveda shampoo and conditioner at all, IMHO. Smelled more like salad dressing than shampoo, but that's just me. Dries out your hair pretty badly too. I'd bring my own next time.Also, I was very grateful to the reviewer who mentioned the parking rates are $36 per day. I believe they have now been increased to $37. At first we thought this was outrageous, but when we called around to other hotels, we found that this was actually fairly standard for the area.Lastly, the location is IDEAL! Right next to market street, Union Square, shops, restaurants, etc.We would definitely stay there again.

<Author>uniceverse
<Content>Great location, great fun... My recent stay at the Palomar has revived my love for the Kimpton Group hotels. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Friendly staff, loved the decor, where's the coffee? I agree with all the other reviewers: this is a great little hotel with very friendly staff. My wife arranged for us to have a room with an extra-long bed, which was a treat -- go for this if you're over 6'4.A few folks note the absence of a coffee maker. This is a huge mistake. I want my caffeine without having to trudge to the lobby. We stayed on the 5th floor, where the pretentious restaurant is. We slept in till ten, and the restaurant was already closed, contrary to advertising. So I threw clothes on, went to the lobby, and there was a crowd around the coffee carafes, and regular was out.If you can provide me with a CD player and music to listen to, you can provide me with a coffee maker. Every Holiday Inn Express has one. It does not detract from your ultra Zen hip coolness to have a friggin' coffee maker in the room!The hotel does not serve lunch and you can't get coffee on demand. This is a great hotel, but it is not full service.

<Author>Okemosian
<Content>Nice, but give me in-room coffee and reasonable wine prices We stayed at the Palomar Nov. 18th-19th. Booked their great rate of $129. The hotel is very beautiful, and the rooms very nicely appointed. My husband enjoyed the tall room with the extra long king bed and high showerhead. Our only gripes were that there are no in-room coffee makers (probably too tacky for their decor), and the wines-by-the-glass were extremely expensive. We don't want to have to get dressed and traipse down to the lobby for morning coffee, or deal with pricey room service in the morning just for a cuppa joe. Sorry. (The Relais-Chateaux hotels have the common sense to put coffee/tea service in the hallways, at least.) And while I appreciate their hand-picked wine list, they could offer more reasonably-priced selections. It's California after all, land of countless great wineries and of course 2-buck Chuck! Pretentious wine lists don't impress me. I'd consider going back if those two issues were addressed.

<Author>Colette
<Content>Beautiful hotel, AWFUL service We stayed at the Palomar after several days in wine country were we stayed at the Carneros Inn (see my review of that great place!). The hotel is beautiful. Our room (a luxury King) was very comfortable with a large jazuzzi tub for two, a view of Market Street and double insulated windows for quiet. We ate at the Fifth Floor where the food is interesting and thoughtful, I would recommend eating here but staying elsewhere. The problem with the hotel is the service. We called for turn down service twice and only got it upon our third request when the housekeeper knocked on our door at 5pm in response to a 7:30 service request. Okay, fine. Later, when we ordered room service quite late at night, it took 50 minutes, arrived cold and the server did not a pen! Our tub would not drain and they never came to fix it so we would have to wedge a comb under the drain lid to keep it up to drain. When we checked out, we asked for a taxi and was directed to a Town Car that would have cost $20 more than a yellow cab. Some people like that but we found it a bit presumptous. Stay here if you like hip surroundings, just need a room and nothing else.

<Content>The Palomar is amazing... The Hotel Palomar was everything I had hoped for- so much that I not sure to begin! I found the Palomar through an air/hotel package for a great price, and we visited from July 15th to the 18th. The Hotel Palomar was one of the best hotels that I have ever stayed at, and I will be staying there again when I return to San Francisco!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Feb of 2004 I loved it. Simply put it was a great hotel in the heart of SF. You are by the Bart Station and the Trolley cars. You are near a Walgreen so if you are missing any of your toiletries or looking for that small snack you can go there in a heart beat.The Lobby is small but it makes it up for its decor and service. The rooms were great. I had plenty of room with a nice view of the city. The noise level was that of a city so I was fine. They had ample closet space and within the closet was a user friendly room safe. The bed linins were soft and the pillows not rock hard or super soft. I had a wonderful good night sleep with their comfy bed. It was very nice to have a mini stereo system that allowed me to play my CDs and they offered Yoga straps, blocks and mats if one wanted to practice yoga along with the program they play on the Hotel TV channel. The bath products were Avada so very user friendly and not to mention great product line. The mini bar was well stocked with great products if one chooses to indulge. The maid service was prompt and changed my linins and towels each day. I ate the 5th restaurant which is rated one of the best in the city. Great food with lots of creativity. They had an extensive wine list which one should not miss. The food was not only presented well but taste was absolutely to die for. The fusion of east and west was well established and melded well. Believe me I have ate my fair share of bad fusion food.Overall this is a great hotel. I would recommend this hotel to anyone.

<Author>Beardsh
<Content>Made my 30th Birthday Special The Palomar was my first destination when visiting the West Coast in February 2004. We stayed for 5 nights and I celebrated my 30th birthday there. We did not eat in the hotel so cannot comment on the food but found it be ideal for our needs, perfectly situated, modern and clean and the staff were excellent. We turned up out of the blue one day with a couple of bicycles we had hired and they kindly helped us to store these for a couple of nights. Staff recommended places to go and eat and were pleasant and helpful at all times particularly when it came for us to hire a car, they provided a map and directions to our next destination - Lake Tahoe. Our last night we booked to stay at the far more expensive Parc 55 hotel and it was appalling. Situated right on the edge of the rough part of town, Tenderloin. If you want a large grand fancy lobby with crap service, small dirty rooms and staff who are uninterested and barely speak English then I strongly recommend Parc 55. If however, you want a clean, stylish and tranquil place to relax then the Palomar will be right up your street. I cannot recommend the hotel highly enough. I wish so much we had booked in here for the last night of our holiday and would not hesitate to return.

<Author>SuzInAZ1950
<Content>Great Suite! We stayed at the lovely Palomar the weekend of 3/14/04 - it was a belated Valentine's Day gift from my husband. In that I love boutique hotels, this was another pleasant surprise in the heart of downtown San Francisco (my fav being the Pan Pacific). These rooms were much larger, and although the bathroom was not as elegant as the Pan, the Fuji bathtub was wonderful - so good for soaking the feet after hitting the streets all day. I filled it to the brim knowing that I was depleting the world of water!! It was very very relaxing. The room was a bit too contemporary for me, but did not detract from my stay.I have two complaints about the room. The way our suite was set up, you couldn't sit on the sofa and look directly at the t.v. You had to lay on the sofa to be head-on with the t.v. Also, there are no coffee making faciliites. In a room that is over $400/night, you would expect to find such a convenience - after all...you get that in the $59/night Best Western!My big gripe with the area, not the hotel, is that you are in downtown San Francisco, and there are few good restaurants around, so it's either order from room service or go to the bistro down the street (and by the way, room service gets its food from the bistro down the street). So if you are going to stay at the Palomar, keep that in mind. You will either have to go to the financial or theater district or go elsewhere. If you DO get to Fisherman's Wharf, eat at Scoma's - they have the best (albeit expensive) seasfood going!I'd stay at the Paloma again, but before I'd go back, I'd stay at the Hotel Monaco - it's sister hotel (both are pet-friendly by the way).BY THE WAY - SKIP THE COURTYARD ROOMS. All you see is 3 other interior walls and you look down through a glass roof into Old Navy. This is a gripe I almost forgot. We got to the hotel early and stowed our luggage and went to get lunch (see note above about eateries in the area) and do some shopping. We hiked all the way to Chinatown before finding any place for lunch - the hotels in the area do not have coffee shops! Anyway, the front desk told us to be back at 2 pm, and we were, and our room still wasn't ready. The staff said that the people were still checking out. They had us wait in the 5th floor loung, very very dark- no coffee pot, no water, no nothing but couches  lounge chairs. 45 minutes later, I sent my husband to complain. The front desk said the couple had spilled something on the carpet  they were cleaning it up, and did we want an interior room instead. DO NOT GET AN INTERIOR ROOM (see note above). If we had been given our exterior room, we would have been able to sit there and watch the St. Patrick's Day parade on Sunday. The view stunk. All in all, maybe I won't go back there again. I think I'll stay down by the Wharf where there's tons of restaurants  things to do (but I STILL loved that bathtub)!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great room, poor service, and fraudulent advertising I stayed at the Hotel Palomar for 6 nights in March. I found a deal for 137/night on Orbitz and I saw on Palomar's website that they offer to match any internet rate and to include with that a free upgrade to the best available room (offer has since changed to best room in next 'tier.' While they honored the rate, the refused to honor the upgrade, even though a quick check on the web showed that better rooms were available. (I read about this exact problem right here on trip-advisor reviews, so I wasn't surprised). They basically said that the room I got WAS an upgrade, because it was an exterior room, instead of an interior room. This is just ridiculous, because their website, on which they promise the upgrade, makes no mention of this distinction. And besides, the deal we were offered said best available room, not slightly better room. When I discussed this problem with Brian Fenwick, the general manager, he was rude and unhelpful (another review on this website makes this same point; take note, Kimpton Group!!). He claimed that the website booking system was incorrect about better rooms being available and that I WAS, in fact, in the best available room. Before speaking with Brian, I had a friend call the front desk and try to book a suite; she was informed that they had several suites available. When I told this to Brian, he said that while the rooms may be available to others for booking, but that they were allotted, so he was unable to upgrade me. This is nonsense. I'm not sure what is more disturbing: that they wouldn't honor the upgrade, or that Brian would tell a bold-faced lie and say the rooms were unavailable. Besides this unpleasantness, the hotel was fine: a nice big room, service once a day (although they say you should get it twice), and a big clean bathroom. Just don't expect the web upgrade deal to be honored.

<Author>termoo
<Content>Very Classy Our whole family recently stayed at the Hotel Palomar in one of their 2-bedroom suites. (January 30) We had a gift certificate from Kimpton Hotels, and decided to splurge with an overnight in San Francisco (though we only live 45 minutes away) when we went to see The Lion King.We were cheerfully greeted by the doorman each time we came and went. In fact, on Saturday, when the staff was different (and less friendly, by the way) my 10-year-old daughter mentioned that she missed that nice door guy.Our room was beautifully decorated and very comfortable. The furnishings, carpet, lamps and accessories were tasteful and sophisticated. All of the artwork on the walls was gorgeous and interesting, and we even had a live palm in the dining area. Two of the kids donned their swim suits and sat in the bathtub as though it were a hot tub. Having such a deep Fuji tub was definitely a treat! We loved looking down on Market St. from our huge windows throughout the suite. There were two free apples and two free bottles of water waiting for us, as well as a VERY well-stocked mini-bar and fridge that we had to quickly keep the kids away from!The exercise room has a nice view of the rooftop garden and an interesting view through the glass ceiling of the Old Navy store that the hotel sits on top of. Although we didn't eat there, the restaurant was quite striking with a very appetizing menu. Someday without the kids...I was very happy with the location and the level of service. We only stayed one night, and I left wanting to stay a few more. I would definitely recommend this as a classy and comfortable place to spend time in San Francisco.

<Content>Palomar is Perfection! From the moment we arrived at the Hotel Palomar we knew we had found a wonderful hotel. Aveda bath products made for a relaxing shower. The second night they upgraded us to a room with a jacuzzi. Because we were out during the day they even moved our luggage for us to the new room. The jacuzzi was large enough for 2 (as was the shower next to it) and it was sooooo relaxing. Each room has a CD player, TV, mini-bar, and lots for business travelers (such as fax  internet). The beds have puffy down pillows and a down comforter so it was very cozy. Everyone from the doormen who opened the door as we rounded the corner towards the hotel to the front desk workers went out of their way to make us feel welcome and pampered. The hotel location is perfect as well since it is just 1 block from the cable car and underground and the buses and street cars stop right at the corner. See's candy being about 1/2 block away was nice too! The Hotel Palomar was the perfect spot to see San Francisco and made for a romantic get-away. I would happily return and heartily recommend it to anyone looking for a place to see the city while being treated like royalty.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great location, but beware! After extensive research, we chose the Palomar hotel for a three day stay just before Thanksgiving. Rates run $175-400, but if you look on sites like Expedia you can get a deal (we paid $119/night) The hotel's own website says that they will match any rate you find on the web, and give you an upgrade to the best room available if you book through them....Do NOT believe them! They honored the rate, but would not upgrade us, even though upgraded rooms and suites were available (we checked through the website). The room was clean and fairly small, but the bed was comfy, and we didn't spend any time in the room anyway. Also, VERY IMPORTANT....parking is $36/day plus $5/day tax=$41/day to park your car.....more than the cost of the rental car! Front desk clerks double as the concierge and are generally useless....they can read off a list of suggested places to see/eat, but have no knowledge of their own. Bottom line.....not bad for $119/night because you are steps from Union Square and a short walk to Chinatown, but if you are used to 5 star service/quality, this isn't the place for you.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Mediocre service but nice rooms If you are a non-smoker like me, make sure you check in early. We booked a non-smoking room with late check in. When we arrived they checked us in but did not tell us we were being put in a smoking room. We got to the room and found a distinct odor of stale smoke in the furniture and bedding - and the windows did not open. Since the hotel was sold out, they refused to move us until the next morning, and the staff were not overly apologetic about the situation. They said non-smoking rooms are not guarenteed to any guests- had I known this I might not have stayed there!! However, to be fair, once we were moved our stay was much more pleasant. The beds are extremely comfy and the rooms are very classy. Unfortunately there is no real lobby to speak of, and I often felt like a number rather than a valued guest. I was in San Francisco for a special occasion with my boyfriend, and was disappointed by the service. I would recommend this hotel to others but would advise you to check in early for a room with a decent view and a room that does not smell like an ashtray.

<Content>great hotel My wife and I stayed at the Palomar for 5 nights starting the Saturday of Labor day weekend. I had done a lot of research and thought this hotel would be the best for us. <Author>Carolina_Girl_in_GA
<Content>Luxury hotel with down-home service After conducting extensive web research, I chose the Palomar for my stay in San Francisco last week on vacation. I found a wonderful deal for the room, but I was concerned my husband and I would be stuck in the broom closet. Thankfully, my fears were unfounded. Staying at the Palomar was overall a lovely experience, during which we were treated as first class guests. I will say, though, that I missed having a real lobby area, and the concierge service was spotty, since the concierge also doubles as a front-desk worker (believe me, the desk can be quite busy at all times of the day). However, all the staff were quite friendly and tried to be helpful in any way. The room was well-decorated, the beds were comfortable, and the towels/bath fixtures were sumptuous. Be sure to take advantage of the Fifth Floor restaurant -- the hotel holds a few tables for hotel guests, so there's no need to try for an impossible-to-get reservation before you go. While pricey, the dining experience is worth it!! The location is prime, close to all public transportation, yet somehow the interior of the hotel managed to be completely sound-proof to the extremely noisy street. Very relaxing environment. Check around on the major travel websites for deals on this hotel, and you won't be disappointed.
